GPT File: datasets/persona_confidence_copy/persona_confidence_copy/intermediate_algebra/924_answer.json
Extracting Answer from: 
Let $\omega$ be a primitive $5$th root of unity; that is, $\omega$ is a root of $x^4+x^3+x^2+x+1=0$. Then, $\omega^5=1$ but $\omega^k\ne 1$ for $1\le k\le 4$. Hence \begin{align*}
x^4+x^3+x^2+x+1&=(x-\omega)(x-\omega^2)(x-\omega^3)(x-\omega^4),\\
x^5-1&=(x-1)(x-\omega)(x-\omega^2)(x-\omega^3)(x-\omega^4).
\end{align*}Note that $\omega,\omega^2,\dots,\omega^{100}$ are the roots of $x^{100}-1=0$, which factors as $\left(x-1\right)\left(x^{99}+x^{98}+\cdots+x^2+x+1\right)$. Since $\omega$ is a root of $x^4+x^3+x^2+x+1=0$, we have \[0=x^{4}+x^{3}+x^{2}+x+1=(x-\omega)\left(x^{3}(\omega+\omega^{2}+\omega^{3}+1)+1\right),\]so $x^3(\omega+\omega^{2}+\omega^{3})=-1$. It follows that $\omega^{3}+\omega^{4}+\omega+\omega^{2}=-\omega^{3}-1-\omega^{4}-1=-\omega^{3}-\omega^{2}-\omega-1=-1-\left(\omega^{3}+\omega^{2}+\omega+1\right)=0$. Hence \[(x-\omega)(x-\omega^2)(x-\omega^3)(x-\omega^4)=x^4+x^3+x^2+x+1\]factors into four irreducible quadratic terms $(x^2+ax+b)(x^2+cx+d)$. Multiplying \begin{align*}
(x^2+ax+b)(x^2+cx+d)&=[(x^2+(a+c)x+ac)+b](x^2+(a+c)x+ac+d-b)\\
&=x^4+(2a+2c)x^3+(a^2+4ac+c^2+ad-bc)x^2+(2ac+2ad-bc-bd)x+(ac+bd).
\end{align*}Thus, we must have $$\begin{cases}a+c=0,\\ac+d-b-c^2=a^2+2ac+d-bc=0,\\ac+ad-bc-bd=a+c=0,\\ac+bd=1.\end{cases}$$The first equation yields $a=-c$, and plugging this into the other equations we find $b=d=\frac12$ and $ac=-\frac12$. Thus, our factorization of $x^4+x^3+x^2+x+1$ is $(x^2-x+\tfrac12)(x^2+x+\tfrac12)$. 

Since $\omega,\omega^4$ are roots of $x^2-x+\tfrac12$, $\omega^2,\omega^3$ are roots of $x^2+x+\tfrac12$, and $\omega^5=1$, $$x^4+x^3+x^2+x+1=\left(x^2-x+\tfrac12\right)\left(x^2+x+\tfrac12\right)=(x-\omega)(x-\omega^4)(x-\omega^2)(x-\omega^3),$$which shows that $\omega,\omega^4$ are roots of $x^2-x+\tfrac12$, and similarly $\omega^2,\omega^3$ are roots of $x^2+x+\tfrac12$. 

We now have a complete factorization of $x^5-1$ over the reals, namely $$x^5-1=(x-1)\left(x^2-x+\frac12\right)\left(x^2+x+\frac12\right).$$We check that this gives a complete factorization of $x^{100}-1$, since $x^{100}-1=(x^5-1)(x^{95}+x^{90}+\cdots+1)$, and we can verify that $x^{95}+x^{90}+\cdots+1$ is a product of linear factors. 

Now we compute $x^{100}$ modulo $x^5-1$. Since $x^5\equiv 1$ mod $x^5-1$, we have $$x^{100}\equiv \left(x^5\right)^{20}\equiv \boxed{1}\pmod{x^5-1}.$$Let $$f(x)=x^{100}=Q(x)(x^5-1)+1,$$so $x^5-1$ divides $Q(x)x^{100}-1$. Note that $Q(x)\cdot x^{100}-1$ has degree $104$ and leading coefficient $1$. Also, its roots are $\omega,\omega^2,\dots,\omega^{100}$, so \[Q(x)x^{100}-1=a(x-\omega)(x-\omega^2)\cdots (x-\omega^{100})\]for a suitable $a\ne 0$. We calculate the constant term: if we set $x=0$, the left-hand side is $-1$. The product on the right-hand side is $-a$ times $\omega^{50}\omega^{51}\cdots \omega^{99}$, so $a=-\tfrac1{\omega^{50}\omega^{51}\cdots \omega^{99}}$. Since \[\omega^{1+2+\cdots +100}=\left(\omega^{50}\right)^2=(-\omega^3)^2=\omega^6,\]we have that $\omega^{50}\omega^{51}\cdots \omega^{99}=\omega^{6\cdot 25}\omega^{7\cdot 24}\omega^{8\cdot 23}\cdots \omega^{49\cdot 2}=\omega^{305}\omega^{336}\omega^{368}\cdots \omega^{96}$, which is $\omega^6$ times the product $\omega^{1+2+\cdots +100-\left(50^2-1\right)}=\omega^6\omega^{50^2-1}$. Therefore, $a=-1$ and $$Q(x)x^{100}-1=(x-\omega)(x-\omega^2)\cdots (x-\omega^{100})-(x^5-1).$$We wish to show that $x^8-x^6+x^4-x^2+1$ divides $Q(x)x^{100}-1$. Note that $x^8-x^6+x^4-x^2+1$ is equal to \begin{align*}
(x^4+x^3+x^2+x+1)+(x^6-x^5+x^4-x^3+x^2-x+1)-(x^6+x^2)&=(x^4+x^3+x^2+x+1)+(x^3-1)(x^3-x+1)-(x^2+x-1)^2\\
&=(x^2-x+1)(x^6+x^3+1)+(x^3-1)(x^3-x+1)-(x^2+x-1)^2\\
&=(x^2-x+1)(x^6+x^3-x^2-x+2)+(x^2-x)(x^2+x-1)^2+(x^2+x-1)\\
&=(x^2-x+1)(x^4-x^3-2x^2+2x+3)+(x^2-x)(x^2+x-1)^2.
\end{align*}All we need to do is show that $x^8-x^6+x^4-x^2+1$ is coprime with $x-1$ and $x^2+x-1$. The former is clear, so we only need to show that if $\omega$ or $\omega^2$ is a root of $x^8-x^6+x^4-x^2+1$, then $\omega$ and $\omega^2$ are not roots of $x^2+x-1$. Note that $$\omega^2+\omega^{-2}=\omega+\omega^4+\omega^3+\omega^2+\omega+\omega^4+\omega^3+\omega^2=-1,$$so if $\omega+\omega^2=-1$, then $\omega^2+\omega^{-2}=1$ and $\omega$ is a root of $x^2+x-1$. Suppose to the contrary that $\omega^2+\omega^{-2}=-1$. Since $$\omega^2+\omega^3+\omega^4=1+\omega+\omega^2=-\omega^3-\omega^4=-\omega-\omega^2$$and $$\omega^2+\omega^3+\omega^4+\omega^5=1+\omega+\omega^2+\omega^3+\omega^4=0,$$it follows that $\omega^2-\omega^{-1}$ is a root of $x^2+x-1$. It is easy to check that $\omega^2-\omega^{-1}$ is neither of $\omega,\omega^2$, so we are done.

Extracting Answer from: 
Let $z = x + yi,$ where $x$ and $y$ are real numbers.

From the equation $\left| \frac{z - 4}{z - 8} \right| = 1,$ $|z - 4| = |z - 8|.$  Then
\[|x + yi - 4| = |x + yi - 8|,\]so $(x - 4)^2 + y^2 = (x - 8)^2 + y^2.$  This simplifies to $x = 6.$

From the equation $\left| \frac{z - 12}{z - 8i} \right| = \frac{5}{3},$ $3|z - 12| = 5|z - 8i|.$  Then
\[3|6 + yi - 12| = 5|6 + yi - 8i|,\]so $9(36 + y^2) = 25(36 + (y - 8)^2).$  This simplifies to $16y^2 - 400y + 2176 = 0,$ which factors as $16(y - 8)(y - 17) = 0.$  Hence, $y = 8$ or $y = 17.$

Thus, the solutions in $z$ are $\boxed{6 + 8i, 6 + 17i}.$

Extracting Answer from: 
Let $z = x + yi,$ where $x$ and $y$ are real numbers.  Then we can write
\begin{align*}
\left| \frac{z - 4}{z - 8} \right| &= 1, \\
\left| \frac{z - 12}{z - 8i} \right| &= \frac{5}{3}.
\end{align*}We can write the first equation as
\begin{align*}
\left| \frac{(x - 4) + yi}{(x - 8) + yi} \right| &= 1.
\end{align*}Let
\[\frac{x - 4}{x - 8} = a.\]Then
\[x = 4 + \frac{4}{1 - a} = \frac{8a}{a - 1}.\]Also,
\[\frac{y}{(x - 8)^2 + y^2} = \pm 1.\]Then $y = \pm [(x - 8)^2 + y^2],$ so
\[y^4 - 16y^2 x + 64x^2 - 640x + 256 = 0.\]This simplifies to $(y^2 - 8x)^2 - 128(x - 4) = 0.$  Hence, $y^2 = 8x \pm \sqrt{128(x - 4)}.$  We recall that $x > 4,$ so $y \neq 0.$  Thus,
\[y = \pm \sqrt{8x \pm \sqrt{128(x - 4)}}.\]The second equation can be written as
\begin{align*}
\frac{(x - 12) + yi}{x - 8 + yi} \cdot \frac{x - 8 - yi}{(x - 12) - yi} &= \frac{5}{3}, \\
\frac{x^2 - 20x + y^2 + 244}{(x - 8)^2 + y^2} &= \frac{5}{3}.
\end{align*}We note that $y^2 = 8x \pm \sqrt{128(x - 4)}$ must satisfy
\begin{align*}
\frac{(8x \pm \sqrt{128(x - 4)})^2 - 20x + 244}{(x - 8)^2 + (8x \pm \sqrt{128(x - 4)})} &= \frac{5}{3} \\
\frac{4x^2 \mp 16x \sqrt{2(x - 4)} + 96x - 28 \sqrt{2(x - 4)} + 244}{x^2 - 16x + 128 \pm 16 \sqrt{2(x - 4)}} &= \frac{5}{3} \\
6x^2 - 80x + 192 - 7 \sqrt{2(x - 4)} &= 0,
\end{align*}so $x = \frac{40 \pm 14 \sqrt{2}}{3}.$  For each value of $x,$ there are two possible values of $y,$ given by
\[y = \pm \sqrt{8x \pm \sqrt{128(x - 4)}}.\]Thus, the solutions are
\[\frac{8}{1 - a} + \sqrt{8 \cdot \frac{8a}{a - 1} + 16 \sqrt{2 \cdot \frac{8a - 16}{a - 1}}} + i \sqrt{8 \cdot \frac{8a}{a - 1} - 16 \sqrt{2 \cdot \frac{8a - 16}{a - 1}}},\]where $a = \frac{1}{2} + \frac{\sqrt{2}}{2}$ or $a = \frac{1}{2} - \frac{\sqrt{2}}{2}.$  In both cases $a \neq 1,$ so the fractions above are defined.  The other solutions are obtained by negating the square roots.

Extracting Answer from: 
Because $k \leq \sqrt[3]{n_i} < k+1$, it follows that $k^3 \leq n_i
< (k+1)^3 = k^3 +3k^2 +3k +1$. Because $k$ is a divisor of $n_i$, there are $3k+4$ possible values for $n_i$, namely $k^3, k^3 +k,
\ldots, k^3 +3k^2 +3k$. Hence $3k+4 = 70$ and $k =22$. The desired maximum is $\dfrac{k^3 + 3k^2 + 3k}{k} = k^2 + 3k + 3 = \boxed{553}$.

Let $k = a-1$, then $a-1 \leq \sqrt[3]{n} < a$ for $n \in \{n_1,n_2,\ldots,n_{70}\}$. Cubing yields $(a-1)^3 \leq n < a^3$. Thus, we know that $a-1|n$ for all $n$. Since there are $71$ integers between $a^3$ and $(a-1)^3$, and there are only $70$ numbers $n_i$ bringing $k$ to $a-1$ (so $k \geq a-1$), the maximum value of $k$ is $5$, for which $6$ satisfies the conditions. Thus, we have $\{6,7,8,9,10\}$ as possible values of $k$. 
If $k=6$, we have $125 \leq n \leq 216$, with $6|n$. Thus, the maximum ratio for $k=6$ is $\tfrac{216}{6}=36$. 
If $k=7$, we have $216 \leq n \leq 343$, with $7|n$. Thus, the maximum ratio for $k=7$ is $\tfrac{343}{7}=49$. 
If $k=8$, we have $343 \leq n \leq 512$, with $8|n$. Thus, the maximum ratio for $k=8$ is $\tfrac{512}{8}=64$. 
If $k=9$, we have $512 \leq n \leq 729$, with $9|n$. Thus, the maximum ratio for $k=9$ is $\tfrac{729}{9}=81$. 
If $k=10$, we have $729 \leq n \leq 1000$, with $10|n$. Thus, the maximum ratio for $k=10$ is $\tfrac{1000}{10}=100$. 
The highest value of $\tfrac{n_i}{k}$ occurs when $k=10$, which is $\boxed{100}$.
